text:
10 stars for sure..This marinade was fabulous.  The only changes were I doubled the recipe and added 3 limes opposed to two(for which I used a glass lemon juicer to get all the juice possible and the pulp), some zest from one lime and instead of garlic powder I went with a fresh clove minced and I also added in some fresh cilantro for our taste preference.  Marinaded for 3 or so hours and I couldn't eat enough pieces.  YUMMY!  The perfect amount of lime and chili taste.  Will be making often this summer.  Thanks!

text:
This recipe was delicious!  I followed it exactly and doubled it so I'd have enough to marinate all the veggies in.  I didn't exactly taste either the chili or the lime, I just tasted that it was delicious!  My husband said he could definitely taste the chili though.  I wouldn't recommend marinating it longer than 4 or 5 hours though b/c I marinated for 4 and the chicken was starting to fall apart...the combination of lime juice and vinegar really breaks down the chicken quickly!

text:
These are definitely more spicy than flavorful and come out very moist.  I marinated these for 6 hours and skewered the chicken with red and green peppers, onions and cherry tomatoes.  Next time I think I'll use crushed garlic vs. garlic powder, and increase the amount of lime juice for a bit more citrus flavor.  Overall, it was very good served with southwestern rice.  If you like spicy food, try this one.

text:
These kabobs were a huge hit at our barbecue--everyone raved. The blend of citrus and spices was wonderful! I marinated the chicken in a Zip-Loc bag for 1 hour. The only thing I did differently was add about 1/2 tsp salt to the marinade, which really helped bring out the flavors. I didn't thread any veggies on the skewers. Instead, I grilled eggplant, zucchini, and red pepper slices separately and served them alongside, accompanied by Caribbean Sweet Potato Salad (also from this site). Thanks for a great new marinade!

text:
I flubbed this so I am giving a 1 star meal (we ate something else for dinner instead), 3 stars to account for my mistake. I marinaded these for about 6 hours (using the juice from one fresh lime) but I still don't think that is long enough to get the good flavor that other reviewers have achieved. I was working w/ a new gas grill & I greatly overcooked them. But, as Michelle said, there wasn't enough flavor & what flavor did come through...was predominately chili powder. I added mushrooms & bell peppers to my skewers in hopes of making it a complete meal but I didn't marinade them (I don't think the lime would complement the mushrooms) & was afraid to add seasonings for fear of competing w/ the chicken marinade. The result...completely flavorless veggies that didn't add a thing to the dish. I don't know if I will ever try this dish again, I'm thinking that even if I had not overcooked it, that it still wouldn't have enough flavor for me ...sorry.

I've made this twice in the last month for different groups of friends/family.  Both times it was very well received.  Neither group were hardcore foodies but both enjoyed it.  Very easy to make. text:
I think the people having flavor issues aren't using enough salt. I tasted the marinade without salt and then added it and the lime flavor just popped out. Delicious recipe. It says "salt to taste" but with the quantities of this marinade you should use at least 1 tsp salt, probably more. Most of the salt is left behind in the marinade when you cook the chicken so too much sodium shouldn't be an issue.

My favorite marinade that I have found so far. I always try new ones, but always come back to this one. Glad I found it 3 years ago. Thought I should share the positive feedback. I found this in search for something different to eat. I shared with my roommates, who were utterly amazed by the chickens flavor. I doubled the oil, vinegar and lime juice, but I only sprinkled a little extra for the spices. Additionally, I sauteed some red onions, green peppers, mushrooms and zucchini, and put a cherry tomato at the end of each kabob. The result was a very clean, unburnt set of kabobs (Except the skewers), and the chicken was still quite most.

It has great potential.   Substituted Vegetable Oil, Apple Cider Vinegar. Added zest of the lime, 2 cloves of Garlic, 1/4 teaspoon Cayenne pepper, Bandania/Shadon Bennie (Cilantro), Soy Sauce, Worcestershire Sauce. Marinated for about 24hours. I also broiled it on a sheet without the skewers. Next time I'll save the marinade and brush the chicken while it is broiling so it doesn't dry out. Love a lot of flavor to my food and couldn't bear having to waste another recipe, so I added extras just in case.  Served with Roasted Veggies (Zucchini, Green Pepper, Red Onion), with some of the spices from the marinade and Teriyaki Sauce. Also Hot Potato and Perfect Rice. Adding some chili powder in both rice and potato for extra flavor. Also added some Pineapple chunks for some sweetness right from the can to the plate.

text:
Great taste!  I skipped the cayenne for my kids' sake and used 2 fresh cloves of garlic since we can't get enough of it around here.  For time, did not do kabobs.  Very tastey, not at all dry as stated by other reviews even though we use great, big Amish chicken breasts.  I suspect it's in how it's marinated & cooked: pierce the chicken all over before coating it & make sure your fire is initially hot to sear & seal in the juices, then turn down your fire & don't overcook it (4-6 minutes per side is all you need).  I liked the suggestion about serving it w/ couscous.  It was a great combo, and the kids thought it was cool.  This recipe made the "keep" list for sure!

Absolutely delicious. I marinated the chicken for about 6hrs I did not include the vegetables in the chicken marinate. I marinated the vegetables in a separate bag and only for 1hr. text:
AMAZING Kabobs! They are citrisy, tangy, and have a little bit of chili zest to them. I did have to substitute the red wine vinegar because I didn't have any. Instead I used balsamic vinegar and that worked great. I also used two lemons and one lime instead of 3 limes because I wanted more marinade to baste the kabobs with once they were on the grill. One caveat: beware of letting the chicken marinate in the citric juice for too long. The chicken will start to break down pretty quickly. Even after just 45 minutes, my chicken pieces were pretty soft.

I made this recipe because I had some limes I needed to use up. The rest of the ingredients I usually have on hand so it wasn't a problem finding them.  I used chicken tenderloins and doubled the recipe because I was cleaning out my fridge. I let some marinate for a few hours (because hubby was hungry) and the remaining overnight. text:
Id give this more than five stars if I could, as long as you use slightly more lime juice.  The chicken tastes fantastic, plus its very moist (even if you leave the chicken on too long).  Be careful about changing the recipe though. Ive made it twice.  The first time I put in too much lime juice (plus I added zest).  The second time I used 1.5 times the amount listed and no zest; that was perfect. The size of limes varies widely, so I recommend a taste test. I used 1/2 tsp of red pepper and fresh garlic. I also prefer chipotle chile powder to regular chili powder.  Finally, if you love it as much as I did, consider making a recipe for six for four people (6 oz chicken/person).

I had planned to grill these kabobs but due to weather conditions, I turned it into a stir fry.  I followed the recipe then added a dash of Worchestershire sauce and a bit of brown sugar as I like a little sweetness with the heat. I browned the chicken in two separate batches, removed from pan,then stirfried peppers, onions, yellow squash and mushrooms. I then added the marinade and brought to a simmer til hot,  added the chicken back in and served over brown rice quinoa combo. It was delicious. Will try for kabobs again using the same veggies and maybe pineapple chunks.

text:
Pretty good marinade!  I loved the lime flavor in this.  I only marinated my chicken for about an hour.  So I could of marinated longer to achieve a stronger flavor on the chicken, but it still gave it nice flavor.  I did use smoked paprika in place of the paprika to give it a nice smokiness.  I didn't taste much of the "chili" flavor in this.  So maybe in place of the chili powder it would be good to use a good chile sauce or I think this would be great with chipotle pepper powder in place of the paprika or part of the chili powder as well.  I love chipotle and lime together.  I do think next time I will use minced garlic in place of the garlic powder, add the zest of a lime, and some cilantro.  At the end of cooking I would also squeeze a lime over top of the chicken and garnish with more cilantro and I think this would make it a 5 star recipe for us!  I used bell peppers, onions, and pineapple to skewer along with the chicken, and served with spanish rice and stewed tomatoes.  Made a great meal.  Thank you for the recipe!

This was "OK." Not terrible but certainly nothing to rave about. FYI, do NOT marinate your chicken for more than a few hours. It will begin to break down due to the acidity from the vinegar and lime juice "cooking" your meat as it marinates! I marinated my chicken for about two hours and when I started to thread it onto my skewers, I noticed the texture was beginning to change. Maybe this will float your boat, but this did nothing for me. Thanks anyways, simmig.

text:
Nice and easy marinade! I used 1 clove fresh garlic instead of garlic powder and left out the onion powder because I didn't have any. I also tossed in about a Tbsp of honey to counter the chili and lime flavor. I was also out of red wine vinegar so I used white wine and marinated the chicken breasts for about 2 hours. It came out good, but the flavor was very subtle. I usually like a stronger flavor on grilled chicken but it was definitely good. I did leave it a bit too long on the grill (a bit dry) so maybe a shorter cooking time would leave a stronger chili-lime flavor. I'd love to try it again and add jalepenoes. Served the chicken with veggies on the grill and also red potatoes that were boiled and then finished on the grill as well. Very nice!

text:
I really had zero expectations for this recipes, I could not think of anything to make and I chose this last minute. Some mods I made to the marinade was that I had no onion powder so I just added in more garlic powder, I also added in 1 tsp chili garlic paste for more chili flavor. I marinated the chicken for 4 hrs and put it on skewers with green pepper and onions and grilled it. When I put the first piece in my mouth I was wowed! I was not expecting such a wonderful melody of flavors. It had great chili flavor with a hint of lime. Although you don't really need any sauce it good on its own,  I found that Thai Spicy dipping sauce took it to a whole other level. Everyone else liked this too, I will definitely make this again, plus is that all the ingredients are ones you will find in your cupboard typically! Served this with tossed romaine orange salad & greek pasta salad, both from this site.
